<p><b>Christian Dannemann Eriksen</b> (<small>Danish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Danish" title="Help:IPA/Danish">[kestjæn eeksn]</a></span>; born 14 February 1992) is a Danish professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as an <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielder</a> for <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> club <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark national team</a>. Eriksen is also capable of playing as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Central_midfielder" title="Midfielder">central midfielder</a> or <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Mezzala" title="Midfielder">mezzala</a> in a 4–3–3 system.
</p><p>Eriksen started his career at Dutch side Ajax, where he won the <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a> in <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Eredivisie" title="2010–11 Eredivisie">2010–11</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Eredivisie" title="2011–12 Eredivisie">2011–12</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Eredivisie" title="2012–13 Eredivisie">2012–13</a> and established himself to comparisons with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Laudrup" title="Michael Laudrup">Michael Laudrup</a> for his traditional <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">number 10 role</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newlaudrup_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newlaudrup-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, Eriksen joined <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham</a> and was named the club's Player of the Year in his debut season.<sup id="cite_ref-spurssigning_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spurssigning-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> During his seven years at the club, he was also named the club's Player of the Year in the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2016–17 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2016–17</a> season and was included in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year_(2010s)#Premier_League_9" title="PFA Team of the Year (2010s)">2017–18 PFA Team of the Year</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2018–19 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2018–19</a> season, Eriksen became only the second player after <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> to record 10+ assists in four successive Premier League seasons and was a key member of the side that reached the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2019 UEFA Champions League Final">2019 UEFA Champions League Final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In January 2020, he signed for Inter Milan.
</p><p>Eriksen made his debut for Denmark in March 2010 and was the youngest player of the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-youngest_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youngest-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In the build-up to the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>, Eriksen played a key-role during the nation's <a href="/wiki/2018_World_Cup_qualification" class="mw-redirect" title="2018 World Cup qualification">qualification campaign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Denmark reached the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_knockout_stage#Round_of_16" title="2018 FIFA World Cup knockout stage">Round of 16</a>, where they were defeated by <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a> after a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-out</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Eriksen has been named the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Football_Player_of_the_Year" title="Danish Football Player of the Year">Danish Football Player of the Year</a> a record five times.
</p>

</ul>
</li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Tottenham_Hotspur"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">Tottenham Hotspur</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career_in_Middelfart_and_Odense">Early career in Middelfart and Odense</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early career in Middelfart and Odense">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Middelfart" title="Middelfart">Middelfart</a>, Denmark, Eriksen followed in his father Thomas' footsteps when he started playing football in the academy of local side, <a href="/wiki/Middelfart_Boldklub" title="Middelfart Boldklub">Middelfart G&amp;BK</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-makings_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-makings-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Eriksen's father was also one of the coaches at the time and in 2004 they helped the youth side finish unbeaten in the local youth championship for the third time in a period of four years.<sup id="cite_ref-makings_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-makings-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The following year, he joined <a href="/wiki/Odense_Boldklub" title="Odense Boldklub">Odense Boldklub</a> who competed in the Danish youth championships and within a year had helped the club to an age-group title. It was at OB that Eriksen first began showing signs of his technical ability, with his dribbling and free-kick techniques lauded by then-coach, Tonny Hermansen.<sup id="cite_ref-makings_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-makings-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> His form at youth level attracted the attention of a number of major European clubs, including the likes of <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Eriksen ultimately underwent trials with both clubs as well as <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF" title="Real Madrid CF">Real Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> and <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a>, but finally decided to move to <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a>, stating, "My first step should not be too big. I knew that playing in the Netherlands would be very good for my development. Then Ajax arrived and that was a fantastic option."<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ajax">Ajax</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ajax">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="2008.E2.80.932010:_Youth_and_first-team_squad"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008–2010:_Youth_and_first-team_squad">2008–2010: Youth and first-team squad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2008–2010: Youth and first-team squad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EriksenAjax3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/EriksenAjax3.jpg/220px-EriksenAjax3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/EriksenAjax3.jpg/330px-EriksenAjax3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/EriksenAjax3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="435" data-file-height="448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EriksenAjax3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eriksen represented <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> between 2008 and 2013 during which time he helped the club to four <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a> titles.</div></div></div>
<p>On 17 October 2008, Eriksen signed a two-and-a-half-year contract with <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>-based club, <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uefastarlet_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uefastarlet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Transfer_fee" class="mw-redirect" title="Transfer fee">transfer fee</a> received by OB was estimated at €1&#160;million (£847,199) while Middelfart also received a sum of €35 000 which they later used to construct a football pitch.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-makings_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-makings-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He worked his way through the youth teams at Ajax and was promoted to the <a href="/wiki/First_team_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="First team (association football)">first team</a> squad in January 2010, where he was given the number 51 shirt.<sup id="cite_ref-uefafaith_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uefafaith-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, he made his first team debut in a 1–1 <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a> with <a href="/wiki/NAC_Breda" title="NAC Breda">NAC Breda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal for Ajax on 25 March in a 6–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Go_Ahead_Eagles" title="Go Ahead Eagles">Go Ahead Eagles</a> in the <a href="/wiki/KNVB_Cup" title="KNVB Cup">Dutch Cup</a> and extended his contract with the club the following month.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> On 6 May, he played in the second match of the final of the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_KNVB_Cup" title="2009–10 KNVB Cup">2009–10 Dutch Cup</a> as Ajax beat <a href="/wiki/Feyenoord" title="Feyenoord">Feyenoord</a> 4–1, prevailing 6–1 on aggregate.<sup id="cite_ref-2010cup_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010cup-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> At the end of his first professional season with the club, Eriksen had played 21 competitive matches, scoring one goal, and had made his international debut for Denmark.<sup id="cite_ref-SW_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SW-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-debut_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debut-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Eriksen's form throughout the campaign earned praise from manager <a href="/wiki/Martin_Jol" title="Martin Jol">Martin Jol</a> who compared him to former youth products <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Sneijder" title="Wesley Sneijder">Wesley Sneijder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rafael_van_der_Vaart" title="Rafael van der Vaart">Rafael van der Vaart</a> as well as Danish legend, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Laudrup" title="Michael Laudrup">Michael Laudrup</a> for his reading of the game in the traditional <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">number 10 role</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uefafaith_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uefafaith-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2010.E2.80.932013:_Breakthrough_years"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–2013:_Breakthrough_years">2010–2013: Breakthrough years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2010–2013: Breakthrough years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Eriksen took the number eight jersey ahead of the following campaign and began the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Eredivisie" title="2010–11 Eredivisie">2010–11 season</a> well, scoring his first Ajax league goal on 29 August 2010 in an away victory over <a href="/wiki/De_Graafschap" title="De Graafschap">De Graafschap</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Over the course of the next few months, he scored his first home goal at the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Arena">Amsterdam Arena</a>, in a 3–0 Cup victory over <a href="/wiki/SC_Veendam" title="SC Veendam">BV Veendam</a>, and his first European goal, in a 3–0 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> win over <a href="/wiki/R.S.C._Anderlecht" title="R.S.C. Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In between the milestone goals, Eriksen was also named <a href="/wiki/Danish_Football_Player_of_the_Year#Danish_Football_Association&#39;s_award" title="Danish Football Player of the Year">Danish Talent of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> His growing capabilities as the team's playmaker saw him become an undisputed starter in the side and he helped Ajax to their first <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Eredivisie" title="2010–11 Eredivisie">Eredivisie title</a> in seven years. At the end of the season he was named Ajax's <a href="/wiki/List_of_AFC_Ajax_records_and_statistics#AFC_Ajax_prize_winners" title="List of AFC Ajax records and statistics">Talent of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ajaxtalent_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ajaxtalent-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> His form throughout the campaign also earned him the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Football_Talent_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Football Talent of the Year">Dutch Football Talent of the Year</a> award which saw him become only the second Danish player to win the award since <a href="/wiki/Jon_Dahl_Tomasson" title="Jon Dahl Tomasson">Jon Dahl Tomasson</a> in 1996. <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff" title="Johan Cruyff">Johan Cruyff</a>, whose panel selected Eriksen for the award, described Eriksen as a typical product of the Danish school and added to previous comparisons between him and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Laudrup" title="Brian Laudrup">Brian</a> and Michael Laudrup."<sup id="cite_ref-talented_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-talented-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EriksenAjax2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/EriksenAjax2.jpg/220px-EriksenAjax2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/EriksenAjax2.jpg/330px-EriksenAjax2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/EriksenAjax2.jpg/440px-EriksenAjax2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="561" data-file-height="502" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EriksenAjax2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eriksen (right) playing for <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> against <a href="/wiki/FC_Spartak_Moscow" title="FC Spartak Moscow">Spartak Moscow</a> in 2011.</div></div></div>
<p>On 18 October 2011, Eriksen scored his first goal in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> when Ajax beat <a href="/wiki/GNK_Dinamo_Zagreb" title="GNK Dinamo Zagreb">Dinamo Zagreb</a> 2–0 in the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2011–12 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In the return fixture the following month, he provided assists to teammates <a href="/wiki/Gregory_van_der_Wiel" title="Gregory van der Wiel">Gregory van der Wiel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siem_de_Jong" title="Siem de Jong">Siem de Jong</a> as Ajax recorded a 4–0 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Five days later he was named <a href="/wiki/Danish_Football_Player_of_the_Year" title="Danish Football Player of the Year">Danish Football Player of the Year</a> in recognition of his role in helping Ajax to the league title the season before and in Denmark's successful <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a> qualification campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Eriksen continued to impress for Ajax and his strong contribution, both in terms of goal and assist returns, helped the club to a second consecutive league title.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Eriksen and Ajax repeated the feat in the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Eredivisie" title="2012–13 Eredivisie">2012–13 season</a> following which he opted not to renew his contract with the club. With only one year remaining on his current contract, Eriksen was permitted to search for a new club and he agreed terms with <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> in England. Eriksen departed Ajax having made 162 appearances across all competitions and scored 32 goals. Along with his league success, he had also featured in three consecutive editions of the <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff_Shield" title="Johan Cruyff Shield">Johan Cruyff Shield</a>, which Ajax won once.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tottenham_Hotspur">Tottenham Hotspur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tottenham Hotspur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="2013.E2.80.932016:_Premier_League_introduction_and_League_Cup_runner-up"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–2016:_Premier_League_introduction_and_League_Cup_runner-up">2013–2016: Premier League introduction and League Cup runner-up</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2013–2016: Premier League introduction and League Cup runner-up">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 30 August 2013, <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> announced that they had completed the transfer of Eriksen from Ajax in a deal believed to be worth £11&#160;million (€12.45&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Eriksen joined the club on the same day as <a href="/wiki/Erik_Lamela" title="Erik Lamela">Erik Lamela</a>, who joined from <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vlad_Chiriche%C8%99" title="Vlad Chiriche">Vlad Chiriche</a>, who joined from <a href="/wiki/FC_Steaua_Bucure%C8%99ti" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Steaua Bucureti">Steaua Bucureti</a>, and took the club's total spending for the <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_football_transfers_summer_2013" title="List of English football transfers summer 2013">2013 summer transfer window</a> to £109.5&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> He made his league debut against <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a> on 14 September 2013 and provided an assist for <a href="/wiki/Gylfi_Sigur%C3%B0sson" title="Gylfi Sigurðsson">Gylfi Sigurðsson</a> in a 2–0 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> After the match, Spurs manager <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Villas-Boas" title="André Villas-Boas">André Villas-Boas</a> commented, "It was a great debut for Christian, he is a pure number 10, a creative player and his individual quality made all the difference."<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christian_Eriksen_v_Arsenal_1314.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Christian_Eriksen_v_Arsenal_1314.jpg/220px-Christian_Eriksen_v_Arsenal_1314.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="292" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Christian_Eriksen_v_Arsenal_1314.jpg/330px-Christian_Eriksen_v_Arsenal_1314.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Christian_Eriksen_v_Arsenal_1314.jpg/440px-Christian_Eriksen_v_Arsenal_1314.jpg 2x" data-file-width="920" data-file-height="1222" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christian_Eriksen_v_Arsenal_1314.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eriksen playing for <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> in 2014</div></div></div>
<p>Five days later, Eriksen "clipped a wonderful dipping shot" over the goalkeeper to score his first Tottenham goal and complete a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Troms%C3%B8_IL" title="Tromsø IL">Tromsø IL</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> He added to his Tottenham goal tally with a goal from a free kick in a 1–1 draw against <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> on Boxing Day 2013, and the second goal in Spurs' 1–2 away win against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> on 1 January 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On 23 March, after goals from <a href="/wiki/Jay_Rodriguez" title="Jay Rodriguez">Jay Rodriguez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lallana" title="Adam Lallana">Adam Lallana</a> had given <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> a 2–0 lead against Tottenham at <a href="/wiki/White_Hart_Lane" title="White Hart Lane">White Hart Lane</a>, Eriksen scored twice to level the score and assisted Sigurðsson to score the winning goal.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> He continued his goalscoring form on 12 April 2014 when he scored a stoppage-time equaliser to help Tottenham come from 3–0 down to draw 3–3 at West Brom.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the season, he had scored ten goals and registered 13 assists across all competitions, won the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Football_Player_of_the_Year" title="Danish Football Player of the Year">Danish Football Player of the Year</a> award and was named Tottenham's Player of the Season.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-POTS_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POTS-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2014–15 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2014–15 campaign</a>, Tottenham appointed <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Pochettino" title="Mauricio Pochettino">Mauricio Pochettino</a> as new club manager after the unsuccessful period under Villas-Boas and interim-manager <a href="/wiki/Tim_Sherwood" title="Tim Sherwood">Tim Sherwood</a>. Between November and December 2014, Eriksen scored late winners against <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a> which he credited to the Argentine manager for raising the team's fitness levels.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the calendar year, Eriksen had scored 12 goals from open play – more than any other player in England – and was soon after awarded his second consecutive Danish Footballer of the Year award.<sup id="cite_ref-DPY_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DPY-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 28 January 2015, Eriksen scored twice in a 2–2 (3–2 aggregate) win over <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> to send Tottenham into the <a href="/wiki/2015_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2015 Football League Cup Final">League Cup Final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> His first goal, a 30-yard curling free kick, was later lauded by former professionals <a href="/wiki/Michael_Owen" title="Michael Owen">Michael Owen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Neville" title="Gary Neville">Gary Neville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The final, played against London rivals <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, took place on 1 March and ended in a 2–0 defeat for Tottenham.<sup id="cite_ref-LC2015_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LC2015-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Eriksen completed the 2014–15 campaign having featured in every Premier League game for Mauricio Pochettino, starting all-but one match, and scored 12 goals across all competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 9 June 2015, amid speculation that he would be joining Manchester United, Eriksen confirmed to Danish media whilst on international duty that he would stay at Tottenham for the foreseeable future and was quoted as saying, "I feel right at home at Tottenham and I haven't thought about leaving yet."<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> He did in fact remain with the club and scored his first goals of the season in October, netting from two free-kicks in a 2–2 draw with Swansea.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In January 2016, Eriksen was once again named Danish Footballer of the Year. In doing so he became the first ever player to win the award in three consecutive years.<sup id="cite_ref-DPY_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DPY-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> He ultimately scored 6 goals and registered 13 assists as Tottenham ended the league season in third place, thereby qualifying for the following season's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-BR_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BR-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2016.E2.80.932020:_Premier_League_runner-up_and_PFA_Team_of_the_Year"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–2020:_Premier_League_runner-up_and_PFA_Team_of_the_Year">2016–2020: Premier League runner-up and PFA Team of the Year</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2016–2020: Premier League runner-up and PFA Team of the Year">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eriksen20162(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Eriksen20162%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Eriksen20162%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Eriksen20162%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Eriksen20162%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Eriksen20162%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Eriksen20162%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="499" data-file-height="528" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eriksen20162(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eriksen striking a <a href="/wiki/Free-kick" class="mw-redirect" title="Free-kick">free-kick</a> while playing for Tottenham in 2016</div></div></div>
<p>Ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League" title="2016–17 Premier League">following season</a>, Eriksen signed a new long-term contract with Tottenham and starred once again for the club, scoring eight goals and assisting a further 15 as the club ended the league campaign as runners-up to champions Chelsea.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Eriksen's tally of assists was bettered only by <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Kevin_De_Bruyne" title="Kevin De Bruyne">Kevin De Bruyne</a> who set up 18 goals for the season.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Eriksen also recorded the joint-most assists in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> and later won the Tottenham Player of the Season award, claiming the award for the second time after previously winning it in his debut season with the club.<sup id="cite_ref-FAC_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAC-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-POTS_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POTS-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Eriksen broke the record for the most goals scored by a Danish player in the Premier League when he scored his 33rd goal in a 3–2 win over <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> on 23 September 2017, surpassing the record previously held by <a href="/wiki/Nicklas_Bendtner" title="Nicklas Bendtner">Nicklas Bendtner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DP_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DP-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> On 9 December, he made his 200th career appearance for Tottenham and marked the occasion by scoring in a 5–1 Premier League win over <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The following month, he scored his 50th goal for the club when he netted after just 11 seconds in the 2–0 league win over Manchester United.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Eriksen's goal was the third-fastest goal ever scored in the Premier League era, bettered only by <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a> and former Spurs captain <a href="/wiki/Ledley_King" title="Ledley King">Ledley King</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> On 17 March 2018, Eriksen scored twice in an <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_FA_Cup" title="2017–18 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> fixture against Swansea to send Spurs to the semi-final for the second season running.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On 1 April, Eriksen scored a 25-yard goal in the away match against Chelsea, helping Tottenham to their first win in 28 years at <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Bridge_(stadium)" title="Stamford Bridge (stadium)">Stamford Bridge</a> in a match that finished 3–1.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, in the reverse fixture against Stoke, Eriksen scored twice to earn Tottenham a 2–1 win. Following the match, however, teammate Harry Kane, who was challenging for the season's <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Golden Boot</a> award, claimed to have made the last touch on the ball for the second goal. Tottenham appealed to the Premier League panel who agreed that the ball touched Kane's shoulder and awarded him the goal.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> On 14 April, Eriksen was named in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a> for the first time, alongside teammates Kane and <a href="/wiki/Jan_Vertonghen" title="Jan Vertonghen">Jan Vertonghen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1718PFA_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1718PFA-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2018–19 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2018–19 season</a>, Eriksen scored his first goal of the season in a Champions League away match against <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The match ended in a 2–1 loss for Tottenham, but in the home game against Inter, Eriksen scored again in the only goal of the game, giving Tottenham a 1–0 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first Premier League goal of the season on 15 December 2018 in the home match against <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a>, a late goal that earned Tottenham a 1–0 win.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> On 31 March, during a 2–1 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, he became only the second player after <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> to record 10+ assists in four successive Premier League seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, on the occasion of his 200th Premier League appearance, he assisted <a href="/wiki/Son_Heung-min" title="Son Heung-min">Son Heung-min</a> for the first ever goal at the new <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_Stadium" title="Tottenham Hotspur Stadium">Tottenham Hotspur Stadium</a> before scoring a goal of his own in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> On 23 April, he scored the winning goal in a 1–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Brighton_%26_Hove_Albion_F.C." title="Brighton &amp; Hove Albion F.C.">Brighton &amp; Hove Albion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Later on, Eriksen played in the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2019 UEFA Champions League Final">2019 UEFA Champions League Final</a>, which resulted a 2–0 defeat for Tottenham against Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inter_Milan">Inter Milan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Inter Milan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 28 January 2020, with his contract at Tottenham set to expire in six months, Eriksen signed a four-and-a-half-year deal with <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> club <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a>, which would net him 10 million euros per season.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> He made his club debut the following day, coming on as a second-half substitute for <a href="/wiki/Alexis_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Alexis Sánchez">Alexis Sánchez</a> in 2–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/ACF_Fiorentina" title="ACF Fiorentina">Fiorentina</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Coppa_Italia" title="2019–20 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> quarter-finals.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> On 20 February 2020, Eriksen scored his first goal for the club, netting the opener in a 2–0 away victory over <a href="/wiki/PFC_Ludogorets_Razgrad" title="PFC Ludogorets Razgrad">Ludogorets Razgrad</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2019–20 UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first Serie A goal on 1 July, in a 6–0 win against <a href="/wiki/Brescia_Calcio" title="Brescia Calcio">Brescia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> On 21 August, Eriksen played in Inter's 2–3 loss against <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2020_UEFA_Europa_League_Final" title="2020 UEFA Europa League Final">2020 Europa League Final</a>, becoming the first player to lose two consecutive finals in the two current major UEFA competitions;<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;nb 1&#93;</a></sup> he had lost the 2019 Champions League Final with Tottenham the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2020, <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Marotta" title="Giuseppe Marotta">Giuseppe Marotta</a> confirmed that Eriksen had been added to the transfer list for 2021; however, his teammate <a href="/wiki/Romelu_Lukaku" title="Romelu Lukaku">Romelu Lukaku</a> had previously hinted that Eriksen's struggles at the Italian club were due to the language barrier.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 26 January 2021, in the dying minutes of Inter's <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_Coppa_Italia" title="2020–21 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> quarter-final match against rivals <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a>, Eriksen was subbed on with the score at 1–1. In the seventh minute of stoppage time and with the game seemingly headed for extra time, Eriksen scored his first goal of the season from a direct free kick to win the match for Inter and send them through to the semi-finals.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Following the match, Inter coach <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Conte" title="Antonio Conte">Antonio Conte</a> said that Eriksen would remain with the club, despite being linked with a winter departure.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_squads">Youth squads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Youth squads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eriksen was called up to the <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_under-17_football_team" title="Denmark national under-17 football team">Denmark national under-17 football team</a> in July 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> and impressed in his debut for the team on 31 July.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, he scored nine goals in 16 games for the U-17s, and was named <a href="/wiki/Danish_Football_Player_of_the_Year#Young_Players_of_the_Year" title="Danish Football Player of the Year">Danish U-17 Talent of the Year</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Football_Association" title="Danish Football Association">Danish FA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dbu_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dbu-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> He was also one of four nominees for the 2008 Danish Talent of the Year award,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> which was won by <a href="/wiki/Mathias_J%C3%B8rgensen" title="Mathias Jørgensen">Mathias Jørgensen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dbu_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dbu-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> He played 27 games for the under-17 team until February 2009. He played a total of eight games for the <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_under-18_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Denmark national under-18 football team">Denmark U-18</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_under-19_football_team" title="Denmark national under-19 football team">Denmark U-19</a> teams during 2009. Eriksen was also called up for the Danish U-21 squad to the European championship in Denmark in 2011, the Danish team only participated in the group stage and Eriksen scored a goal against Belarus.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior_squad">Senior squad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Senior squad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eriksen_Euro_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Eriksen_Euro_2012.jpg/220px-Eriksen_Euro_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/07/Eriksen_Euro_2012.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="328" data-file-height="422" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eriksen_Euro_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eriksen playing for <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a> at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a></div></div></div>
<p>Eriksen received his first senior Denmark call-up in February 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> making his debut in Denmark's friendly match against <a href="/wiki/Austria_national_football_team" title="Austria national football team">Austria</a> in March,<sup id="cite_ref-debut_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debut-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> to become Denmark's fourth youngest full international, being the youngest debutant since Michael Laudrup.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 28 May 2010, Denmark coach <a href="/wiki/Morten_Olsen" title="Morten Olsen">Morten Olsen</a> announced that Eriksen would be part of the final squad of 23 participating in the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a> in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> He was the youngest player participating in the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-youngest_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youngest-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-youngest2_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youngest2-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> At the World Cup, Eriksen played two matches, against the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_football_team" title="Japan national football team">Japan</a>, but Denmark were unable to progress beyond the group stage.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 9 February 2011, in a 2–1 friendly loss at home against <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>, Eriksen was named <a href="/wiki/Man_of_the_match" class="mw-redirect" title="Man of the match">man of the match</a>, and was praised for his performance by a number of prominent footballing figures, including <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> star <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard" title="Frank Lampard">Frank Lampard</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Man Utd star <a href="/wiki/Rio_Ferdinand" title="Rio Ferdinand">Rio Ferdinand</a> (on Twitter),<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> manager Morten Olsen and several media experts in Denmark and England.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> On 4 June 2011, Eriksen scored his first national team goal to give Denmark a 2–0 lead over <a href="/wiki/Iceland_national_football_team" title="Iceland national football team">Iceland</a> in their <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012_qualifying_Group_H" title="UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying Group H">Euro 2012 qualifier</a>. In doing so, he became the youngest Danish player ever to score a goal in European qualification, being nine days younger than Michael Laudrup when he scored his first goal in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_and_tournament">2018 FIFA World Cup qualification and tournament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2018 FIFA World Cup qualification and tournament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the build-up to the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>, Denmark were drawn in <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_E" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group E">UEFA Group E</a> alongside the likes of <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_football_team" title="Romania national football team">Romania</a>. Eriksen played a key-role during the nation's qualification campaign during which time he scored eight goals to earn Denmark a play-off against the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The first leg of the play-off ended in a 0–0 home draw before Eriksen netted a <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Aviva_Stadium" title="Aviva Stadium">Aviva Stadium</a> in a 5–1 win to earn Denmark a spot at the World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Eriksen's treble took his tally to 11 goals for the qualification campaign, bettered only by Poland's <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lewandowski" title="Robert Lewandowski">Robert Lewandowski</a> (16) and <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> (15) in Europe, and earned the praise of national team manager <a href="/wiki/%C3%85ge_Hareide" title="Åge Hareide">Åge Hareide</a> who stated that Eriksen was one of the top 10 players in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Denmark's opening match at the tournament, Eriksen assisted <a href="/wiki/Yussuf_Poulsen" title="Yussuf Poulsen">Yussuf Poulsen</a> for the only goal in a 1–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Peru_national_football_team" title="Peru national football team">Peru</a> before scoring his first goal for the tournament in the 1–1 draw with <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australia</a> the following week.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Denmark ultimately progressed from their <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_C" title="2018 FIFA World Cup Group C">group</a> after which they were drawn with <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_knockout_stage#Round_of_16" title="2018 FIFA World Cup knockout stage">Round of 16</a>. There they were defeated after a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-out</a>, with Eriksen being one of three players to have his spot-kick saved by Croatia goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Danijel_Suba%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Danijel Subaši">Danijel Subaši</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="UEFA_Nations_League">UEFA Nations League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: UEFA Nations League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 9 September 2018, Eriksen scored twice in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales</a> to lead Denmark to victory in the nation's inaugural <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_UEFA_Nations_League_B" title="2018–19 UEFA Nations League B">2018–19 UEFA Nations League B</a> match.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> On 14 October 2020, Eriksen played his 100th match for Denmark, in which he scored a penalty in a 1–0 away win against <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_UEFA_Nations_League_A" title="2020–21 UEFA Nations League A">2020–21 UEFA Nations League A</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;nb 2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Described as a "classic number ten" in the media, Eriksen's favoured position is in a free role in the centre of the pitch as an attacking midfielder behind the forwards; however, he is a tactically intelligent and versatile player, who is also capable of playing as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Central_midfielder" title="Midfielder">central midfielder</a> or <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Mezzala" title="Midfielder">mezzala</a> in a 4–3–3 system (as was the case during his first years with Ajax), and even as a right <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">winger</a> in a 4–2–3–1 formation, although he has also been used on the left flank on occasion, and is even capable of playing as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Second_striker" title="Forward (association football)">second striker</a>. Gifted with excellent vision, passing range, <a href="/wiki/Cross_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cross (football)">crossing</a> accuracy, set-piece delivery, creativity, technical skills, movement, and an ability to read the game, as well as good balance and co-ordination, he is highly regarded by pundits for his ability to orchestrate attacking moves for his team with his distribution, create or exploit spaces with his runs, and provide assists to his teammates, which makes him an excellent <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a> and creator. He is also known for his eye for goal from midfield, and for his ability to strike the ball with power and accuracy with either foot, despite being naturally right-footed, in particular from distance; moreover, he has also established himself as a <a href="/wiki/Direct_free_kick" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct free kick">free kick</a> specialist. A talented and hard-working player, his creative playing style, nationality, and role on the pitch has led pundits to compare him to compatriots Michael and Brian Laudrup, who were two of his major influences in his youth, as well as Wesley Sneijder and Rafael van der Vaart; Eriksen has also cited <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Totti" title="Francesco Totti">Francesco Totti</a> as an inspiration.<sup id="cite_ref-style_of_play_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-style_of_play-114">&#91;nb 3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Eriksen lives with his girlfriend Sabrina Kvist Jensen,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Their first child, Alfred, was born on 4 June 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> He had another child who was born in December 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> His younger sister <a href="/wiki/Louise_Eriksen" title="Louise Eriksen">Louise Eriksen</a> (born 1995) also plays football and is the captain for <a href="/wiki/KoldingQ" title="KoldingQ">KoldingQ</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Elitedivisionen" title="Elitedivisionen">Elitedivisionen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Eriksen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1011085734"/><div class="reflist">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-76">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a> was the first player to lose two consecutive European club finals in two different competitions (with <a href="/wiki/FC_Girondins_de_Bordeaux" title="FC Girondins de Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1996_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="1996 UEFA Cup Final">1996 UEFA Cup Final</a> and with <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1997_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1997 UEFA Champions League Final">1997 UEFA Champions League Final</a>).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-103"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-103">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">10 Danish players have reached 100 caps as of 2020. Christian Eriksen is the youngest at 28 years and 243 days.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The first Dane to reach 100 caps was <a href="/wiki/Morten_Olsen" title="Morten Olsen">Morten Olsen</a> in 1989. He has also 100 caps as manager for the Danish national team (the first in the world to have done both).<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The record for most caps for Denmark is 129 and belongs to <a href="/wiki/Peter_Schmeichel" title="Peter Schmeichel">Peter Schmeichel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-style_of_play-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-style_of_play_114-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See<sup id="cite_ref-makings_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-makings-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uefafaith_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uefafaith-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-talented_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-talented-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Goal1-King_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goal1-King-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
